[Core Map Type and Creation](#core-map-type-and-creation)\n2. [CRUD Operations](#crud-operations)\n3. [Iteration and Dumping](#iteration-and-dumping)\n4. [Pinning and Persistence](#pinning-and-persistence)\n5. [Key/Value Interfaces](#keyvalue-interfaces)\n6. [Event System](#event-system)\n7. [Collection Loading](#collection-loading)\n\n---\n\n## Core Map Type and Creation\n\n### Map Struct\n\nThe `Map` struct represents a BPF map in user space. It provides methods to interact with kernel eBPF maps and includes features for caching, events, and persistence.\n\n### Map Creation Functions\n\n#### `NewMap(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue, maxEntries int, flags uint32) *Map`\n\nCreates a new Map instance with the specified parameters.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `name`: The name of the map (used for pinning)\n- `mapType`: Type of eBPF map (Hash, LRUHash, Array, PerCPUHash, etc.)\n- `mapKey`: A MapKey implementation defining the key structure\n- `mapValue`: A MapValue implementation defining the value structure\n- `maxEntries`: Maximum number of entries the map can hold\n- `flags`: eBPF map creation flags (e.g., `BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC`)\n\n**Returns:** A new Map instance in uninitialized state (not yet opened/created)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nkey := &MyKey{}\nvalue := &MyValue{}\nm := NewMap(\"cilium_my_map\",\n    ebpf.Hash,\n    key,\n    value,\n    10000,\n    unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC,\n)\n```\n\n#### `NewMapWithInnerSpec(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue, maxEntries int, flags uint32, innerSpec *ebpf.MapSpec) *Map`\n\nCreates a new Map with an inner map specification. Used for maps-of-maps or maps-of-programs.\n\n**Parameters:** Same as `NewMap`, plus:\n- `innerSpec`: The specification for the inner map\n\n#### `OpenMap(pinPath string, key MapKey, value MapValue) (*Map, error)`\n\nOpens an existing pinned map from the filesystem.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `pinPath`: Absolute path to the pinned map file\n- `key`: A MapKey implementation matching the map's key type\n- `value`: A MapValue implementation matching the map's value type\n\n**Returns:** An open Map instance, or an error if the map doesn't exist or is incompatible\n\n**Requirements:**\n- `pinPath` must be an absolute path\n- The pinned map must have compatible key and value sizes\n\n### Map Lifecycle Operations\n\n#### `Open() error`\n\nOpens an already-pinned map on the filesystem. All calls are serialized by internal locking.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns immediately if the map is already open\n- Loads the map from the pinned path\n- Returns error if map does not exist at the pinned path\n\n#### `OpenOrCreate() error`\n\nAttempts to open a pinned map, or creates a new one if it doesn't exist.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- If map exists on filesystem: loads it and verifies compatibility\n- If map doesn't exist: creates a new one and pins it\n- If existing map is incompatible (different type, key/value size, etc.): deletes it and creates a new one\n- If map is marked as non-persistent: always recreates (does not attempt to load)\n\n**Important:** Returns immediately if the map is already open.\n\n#### `CreateUnpinned() error`\n\nCreates a new map in the kernel without pinning it to the filesystem.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Creates the map in memory only\n- No persistence across restarts\n- Useful for temporary maps or when persistence is managed externally\n\n#### `Create() error`\n\nCreates or opens the map, then immediately closes it.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Equivalent to calling `OpenOrCreate()` followed by `Close()`\n- Useful for just ensuring the map exists without keeping it open\n\n#### `Recreate() error`\n\nRemoves the pinned map and recreates it from scratch.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Removes any existing pin at the map's path\n- Creates a fresh map\n- Re-pins the new map\n- Returns error if map is already open\n\n**Use case:** Clearing all map data when an incompatible state is detected\n\n#### `Close() error`\n\nCloses the map and releases kernel resources.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Closes the underlying eBPF map file descriptor\n- Stops any background error resolver if enabled\n- Does not remove the pinned map from filesystem\n- Safe to call multiple times\n\n---\n\n## CRUD Operations\n\nAll CRUD operations require the map to be open. They will automatically call `Open()` if needed, except for locked operations which assume `Open()` has been called.\n\n### Read Operations\n\n#### `Lookup(key MapKey) (MapValue, error)`\n\nLooks up a single value in the map.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to look up\n\n**Returns:** A new instance of the value type, or an error\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns a new MapValue instance for each call\n- Returns `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` if key is not found\n- Thread-safe\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nval, err := m.Lookup(&MyKey{ID: 42})\nif err != nil {\n    if errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n        // Key not found\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Write Operations\n\n#### `Update(key MapKey, value MapValue) error`\n\nInserts or updates a value in the map.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to insert/update\n- `value`: The value to store\n\n**Returns:** An error if the operation fails\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Creates or updates the entry atomically\n- Thread-safe (serialized by internal lock)\n- If caching is enabled, updates the cache entry\n- If caching is enabled and update fails, schedules error resolver to retry\n- Records update events if event buffer is enabled\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nerr := m.Update(&MyKey{ID: 42}, &MyValue{Data: 100})\n```\n\n### Delete Operations\n\n#### `Delete(key MapKey) error`\n\nDeletes an entry from the map.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to delete\n\n**Returns:** An error if the key doesn't exist or operation fails\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Removes the entry atomically\n- Thread-safe\n- Returns error if key doesn't exist\n- Updates cache if enabled\n- Records delete event if event buffer is enabled\n\n#### `SilentDelete(key MapKey) (bool, error)`\n\nDeletes an entry from the map, ignoring missing keys.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to delete\n\n**Returns:** (true if deleted, false if not found, error)\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Same as Delete() but returns (false, nil) instead of error if key is not found\n- Useful for cleanup operations where missing entries are acceptable\n\n#### `DeleteLocked(key MapKey) error`\n\nDeletes a map entry when the map lock is already held.\n\n**Important Requirements:**\n- **Must only be called from within a DumpCallback** to avoid deadlocks\n- Assumes `m.lock` is already acquired for writing\n- Used when you need to delete entries while iterating the map\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nm.DumpWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    if shouldDelete(key) {\n        m.DeleteLocked(key) // Safe because callback holds the lock\n    }\n})\n```\n\n#### `DeleteAll() error`\n\nDeletes all entries from the map by iterating and deleting individually.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Iterates through all entries and deletes each one\n- Updates cache for each deletion\n- Records a single MapDeleteAll event after completion\n- Entries added during iteration may survive the deletion\n- Thread-safe\n\n**Warning:** Not suitable for very large maps as it iterates every entry. For production clearing, consider `ClearAll()` (if events are not needed).\n\n#### `ClearAll() error`\n\nClears all entries by updating them with empty values instead of deleting.\n\n**Restrictions:**\n- Cannot be used if events buffer is enabled\n- Cannot be used if value cache is enabled\n\n**Behavior:**\n- More efficient than DeleteAll for very large maps\n- Does not record events\n- Thread-safe\n\n### Batch Operations\n\n#### `BatchLookup(cursor *ebpf.MapBatchCursor, keysOut, valuesOut any, opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) (int, error)`\n\nPerforms a batch lookup of multiple entries.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cursor`: Cursor for iteration (persists state across calls)\n- `keysOut`: Pre-allocated slice to receive keys\n- `valuesOut`: Pre-allocated slice to receive values\n- `opts`: Optional batch options\n\n**Returns:** Number of entries read, and error\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Direct wrapper around the underlying eBPF batch lookup\n- More efficient for reading large numbers of entries\n- Returns `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` when end of map is reached\n- May return `unix.ENOSPC` if buffer is too small for LRU hash maps\n\n**Use Case:** Use `BatchIterator` instead for easier iteration with automatic retry logic\n\n#### `BatchCount() (int, error)`\n\nReturns the total number of elements in the map using batch lookup.\n\n**Restrictions:**\n- Only works on Hash, LRUHash, and LPMTrie maps\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Iterates entire map to count entries\n- Automatically handles ENOSPC by doubling buffer size (up to 3 retries)\n- Returns error if max retries exceeded\n\n### Per-CPU Operations\n\n#### `DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error`\n\nIterates over a per-CPU map, calling the callback for each key with all CPU values.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cb`: Callback function receiving key and slice of values from all CPUs\n\n**Type Definition:**\n```go\ntype DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n```\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Only works with per-CPU map types (PerCPUHash, PerCPUArray, LRUCPUHash, PerCPUCGroupStorage)\n- Callback receives a slice of MapValue instances (one per CPU)\n- Thread-safe\n- Value instances are fresh for each callback\n\n**Requirement:** Value type must implement `MapPerCPUValue` interface\n\n---\n\n## Iteration and Dumping\n\n### Callback-Based Iteration\n\n#### `DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error`\n\nIterates over all map entries, calling the callback for each entry.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cb`: Callback function receiving key and value\n\n**Type Definition:**\n```go\ntype DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\n```\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Iterates using the ebpf-go Iterator\n- Calls callback for each entry\n- Callback receives fresh MapValue instances\n- Thread-safe (read-lock held during iteration)\n\n**Important:** Callbacks should not perform operations that require write access to the map\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nerr := m.DumpWithCallback(func(key, value MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"Key: %v, Value: %v\\n\", key, value)\n})\n```\n\n#### `DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error`\n\nLike `DumpWithCallback`, but returns without error if map doesn't exist.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns nil if map doesn't exist\n- Otherwise identical to DumpWithCallback\n\n#### `DumpIfExists(hash map[string][]string) error`\n\nDumps map contents into a Go map, if the map exists.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Converts keys and values to strings using String() method\n- Returns nil if map doesn't exist\n- Returns error if dump fails\n\n#### `Dump(hash map[string][]string) error`\n\nDumps all map entries into a Go map using string representations.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `hash`: Pre-allocated map to receive string-formatted entries\n- Keys are map keys, values are slices of string values\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Iterates entire map using DumpWithCallback\n- Converts keys/values to strings\n- Multiple values for same key are appended to the slice\n- Thread-safe\n\n### Reliable Iteration with Backtracking\n\n#### `DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error`\n\nIterates over the map with support for concurrent modifications during iteration.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cb`: Callback function receiving key and value\n- `stats`: DumpStats instance to track iteration metrics\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Handles keys deleted during iteration by backtracking to recently seen keys\n- Handles iteration restart if all keys are deleted during traversal\n- Caps iteration at 4x the maximum map size to prevent infinite loops\n- Holds map lock during iteration (required for callbacks with map operations)\n- Returns `ErrMaxLookup` if iteration limit exceeded\n\n**Thread-Safety:** Holds write lock during iteration - callbacks can perform map operations\n\n**Use Case:** When iterating maps that are actively modified by other goroutines\n\n**DumpStats Fields:**\n- `Started`: Timestamp when iteration started\n- `Finished`: Timestamp when iteration completed\n- `Lookup`: Total number of key lookups\n- `LookupFailed`: Number of failed lookups\n- `KeyFallback`: Times we fell back to previous key\n- `Interrupted`: Times iteration was interrupted\n- `MaxEntries`: Maximum map capacity\n- `Completed`: Whether iteration finished successfully\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nstats := NewDumpStats(m)\nerr := m.DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb, stats)\nif err == ErrMaxLookup {\n    // Map too volatile, consider alternative approach\n}\nfmt.Printf(\"Completed: %v, Lookups: %d\\n\", stats.Completed, stats.Lookup)\n```\n\n### Batch Iterator\n\n#### `NewBatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]`\n\nCreates a new batch iterator for efficient iteration using the batch API.\n\n**Type Parameters:**\n- `KT`: Key type\n- `VT`: Value type\n- `KP`: Pointer to key type (must implement MapKey)\n- `VP`: Pointer to value type (must implement MapValue)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype MyKey struct { ID uint32 }\ntype MyValue struct { Data uint32 }\n\n// Implement MapKey and MapValue interfaces\nfunc (k *MyKey) String() string { return fmt.Sprintf(\"key=%d\", k.ID) }\nfunc (k *MyKey) New() MapKey { return &MyKey{} }\nfunc (v *MyValue) String() string { return fmt.Sprintf(\"val=%d\", v.Data) }\nfunc (v *MyValue) New() MapValue { return &MyValue{} }\n\n// Create iterator\niter := NewBatchIterator[MyKey, MyValue](m)\n\n// Iterate\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n    // k is *MyKey, v is *MyValue\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    // Handle error\n}\n```\n\n#### `BatchIterator.IterateAll(ctx context.Context, opts ...BatchIteratorOpt) iter.Seq2[KP, VP]`\n\nReturns an iterator sequence for batch-based iteration.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Automatically determines starting chunk size based on map size\n- Handles ENOSPC by doubling buffer size and retrying (default: 3 retries)\n- Respects context cancellation\n- Returns all key-value pairs as pointers\n- Resets internal state on each call (can be reused)\n\n**Restrictions:**\n- Only works on Hash, LRUHash, and LPMTrie maps\n\n**Options:**\n- `WithEBPFBatchOpts(*ebpf.BatchOptions)`: Override batch options\n- `WithMaxRetries(uint32)`: Set max retries for ENOSPC (default: 3)\n- `WithStartingChunkSize(int)`: Set initial batch size (default: computed)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\niter := NewBatchIterator[MyKey, MyValue](m)\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx, WithMaxRetries(5)) {\n    process(k, v)\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Iteration failed: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n#### `BatchIterator.Err() error`\n\nReturns any error encountered during the previous `IterateAll()` call.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Error is reset when `IterateAll()` is called again\n- Reusing the iterator resets the error\n\n#### Helper Functions\n\n`CountAll[KT, VT, KP, VP](ctx context.Context, iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) (int, error)`\n\nCounts all entries using the batch iterator.\n\n---\n\n## Pinning and Persistence\n\n### Pinning Concepts\n\n**Pinned maps** are persisted to the BPF filesystem and survive process restarts. **Unpinned maps** exist only in kernel memory and are destroyed when the process exits.\n\n### Pin/Unpin Operations\n\n#### `Unpin() error`\n\nUnpins (removes) the map from the BPF filesystem.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Removes the pinned map file\n- The map remains open and functional until explicitly closed\n- The next process loading the map will create a new one\n\n#### `UnpinIfExists() error`\n\nUnpins the map only if it exists, returning no error if it doesn't.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Checks if map exists first\n- Returns nil if map doesn't exist\n- Otherwise identical to Unpin()\n\n### BPF Filesystem Paths\n\n#### `BPFFSRoot() string`\n\nReturns the root path where the BPF filesystem is mounted (typically `/sys/fs/bpf`).\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns the global bpffsRoot path\n- Locked after first access to prevent misconfiguration\n\n#### `CiliumPath() string`\n\nReturns the BPF filesystem path for Cilium object pins (typically `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium`).\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns filepath joined with BPFFSRoot\n- Locked after first access\n\n#### `MapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string) string`\n\nReturns the filesystem path where a map with the given name will be pinned.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Differs based on component (Cilium agent vs others)\n- For Cilium agent: returns path in TCGlobalsPath\n- For others: derives path from mount info\n\n#### `TCGlobalsPath() string`\n\nReturns the legacy TC globals path for map pins (typically `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals`).\n\n#### `LocalMapName(name string, id uint16) string`\n\nReturns a name for a map that is local to a specific ID.\n\n**Format:** `{name}{id:05d}` (zero-padded 5-digit ID)\n\n#### `LocalMapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string, id uint16) string`\n\nReturns the filesystem path for a locally-scoped map.\n\n### Map Persistence Behavior\n\n**OpenOrCreate() behavior:**\n- Pinned maps (default): Loads from pin path if compatible, recreates if incompatible\n- Non-persistent maps: Always recreates, ignoring any existing pin\n- Map spec Pinning flag: Determines if map is pinned during creation\n\n**CreateUnpinned() behavior:**\n- Creates map without pinning (exists only in memory)\n- Useful for temporary maps\n\n---\n\n## Key/Value Interfaces\n\n### MapKey Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapKey interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n\n    // New must return a pointer to a new MapKey instance.\n    New() MapKey\n}\n```\n\n**Requirements:**\n- Must implement `String() string` (via Stringer)\n- `New()` must return a fresh pointer instance\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype EndpointKey struct {\n    IP        [16]byte\n    Family    uint8\n    Key       uint8\n    ClusterID uint16\n}\n\nfunc (k EndpointKey) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"IP:%v, Family:%d\", k.IP, k.Family)\n}\n\nfunc (k *EndpointKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &EndpointKey{}\n}\n```\n\n### MapValue Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapValue interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n\n    // New must return a pointer to a new MapValue instance.\n    New() MapValue\n}\n```\n\n**Requirements:**\n- Must implement `String() string`\n- `New()` must return a fresh pointer instance\n\n### MapPerCPUValue Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapPerCPUValue interface {\n    MapValue\n\n    // NewSlice must return a pointer to a slice of structs implementing MapValue.\n    NewSlice() any\n}\n```\n\n**Additional Requirement:**\n- `NewSlice()` returns a pointer to a slice containing MapValue instances (one per CPU)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype MyValue struct {\n    Counter uint64\n}\n\ntype MyValueSlice []MyValue\n\nfunc (v *MyValue) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"counter=%d\", v.Counter)\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyValue) New() MapValue {\n    return &MyValue{}\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyValue) NewSlice() any {\n    s := make(MyValueSlice, 0)\n    return &s\n}\n```\n\n### EndpointKey Example\n\nEndpointKey is a concrete example implementing MapKey:\n\n```go\ntype EndpointKey struct {\n    IP        types.IPv6\n    Family    uint8\n    Key       uint8\n    ClusterID uint16\n}\n\n// Supports both IPv4 (in lowest 4 bytes) and IPv6\n// Family: 1 for IPv4, 2 for IPv6\n\nfunc (k EndpointKey) String() string {\n    // Returns string representation like \"10.0.0.1:0\"\n}\n\nfunc (k *EndpointKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &EndpointKey{}\n}\n\nfunc NewEndpointKey(addr netip.Addr, clusterID uint16) EndpointKey {\n    // Auto-detects address family and constructs key\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Event System\n\nEvents provide a way to track map modifications in real-time without polling. Maps record update, delete, and bulk-delete operations to a bounded circular buffer.\n\n### Event Types\n\n#### Action Enum\n\n```go\ntype Action uint8\n\nconst (\n    MapUpdate  Action = iota  // Single entry updated\n    MapDelete                  // Single entry deleted\n    MapDeleteAll               // Bulk delete (aggregated)\n)\n```\n\n#### Event Struct\n\n```go\ntype Event struct {\n    Timestamp time.Time  // When the event occurred\n    // Contains Action, Key, Value, DesiredAction, LastError fields\n}\n```\n\n**Methods:**\n- `GetAction() string`: Returns action as string (\"update\", \"delete\", \"delete-all\")\n- `GetKey() string`: Returns string representation of key\n- `GetValue() string`: Returns string representation of value\n- `GetLastError() error`: Returns last error (for failed operations)\n- `GetDesiredAction() DesiredAction`: Returns desired action enum\n\n### Event Subscription\n\n#### `DumpAndSubscribe(ctx context.Context, callback EventCallbackFunc, follow bool)`\n\nDumps existing events and optionally subscribes to future events.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `ctx`: Context for controlling subscription lifetime\n- `callback`: Function called for each event\n- `follow`: If true, continues receiving new events after dump\n\n**Type Definition:**\n```go\ntype EventCallbackFunc func(Event)\n```\n\n**Behavior:**\n- First calls callback for all existing events in buffer\n- If follow=true, subscribes to future events via stream\n- Subscription ends when context is cancelled\n- Events in buffer are filtered by TTL (expired events excluded)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\ndefer cancel()\n\nm.DumpAndSubscribe(ctx, func(e Event) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"%s: %s -> %s\\n\", e.GetAction(), e.GetKey(), e.GetValue())\n}, true)\n\n// Later...\ncancel() // Stop receiving events\n```\n\n#### `IsEventsEnabled() bool`\n\nReturns whether the event buffer is enabled for this map.\n\n### Enabling Events\n\n#### `WithEvents(config option.BPFEventBufferConfig) *Map`\n\nEnables event buffering on the map.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `config.Enabled`: Whether to enable event buffer\n- `config.MaxSize`: Maximum number of events to buffer\n- `config.TTL`: How long to keep events (0 = keep forever)\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Creates a bounded circular buffer for events\n- Automatically garbage collects expired events if TTL > 0\n- Uses approximately 100MB per million capacity\n- Returns immediately if Enabled=false\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"my_map\", ebpf.Hash, key, value, 10000, 0).\n    WithEvents(option.BPFEventBufferConfig{\n        Enabled: true,\n        MaxSize: 10000,\n        TTL:     5 * time.Minute,\n    }).\n    OpenOrCreate()\n```\n\n### DesiredAction Enum\n\n```go\ntype DesiredAction uint8\n\nconst (\n    OK     DesiredAction = iota  // Entry is in sync\n    Insert                        // Entry needs to be created/updated\n    Delete                        // Entry needs to be deleted\n)\n```\n\n**Used by:** Cache and event system to track synchronization state\n\n---\n\n## Collection Loading\n\nThe collection loading system handles loading eBPF programs and maps from ELF files compiled with eBPF C code.\n\n### Collection Loading Functions\n\n#### `LoadAndAssign(logger *slog.Logger, to any, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec, opts *CollectionOptions) (func() error, error)`\n\nLoads an eBPF collection and assigns it to the provided struct.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `logger`: Logger for debug output\n- `to`: Target struct to assign loaded objects to (typically contains *Map fields)\n- `spec`: The compiled eBPF collection specification\n- `opts`: Load options\n\n**Returns:**\n- Commit function: must be called after attaching programs to hooks\n- Error: if loading failed\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Analyzes struct fields to determine which objects to keep\n- Loads the collection into the kernel\n- Assigns maps and programs to matching struct fields\n- Returns a commit function for finalizing pins\n\n**Commit Function:**\n- Must be called after all programs are attached to their hooks\n- Commits any map pins that were marked for replacement\n- When multiple programs from same ELF are attached, call commit only after all are attached\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype Objects struct {\n    Map1 *bpf.Map `ebpf:\"map_name_1\"`\n    Map2 *bpf.Map `ebpf:\"map_name_2\"`\n    Prog *ebpf.Program `ebpf:\"xdp_prog\"`\n}\n\nspec, err := ebpf.LoadCollectionSpec(\"program.o\")\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n\nobj := &Objects{}\ncommit, err := bpf.LoadAndAssign(logger, obj, spec, nil)\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n\n// Attach programs...\nerr = syscall.BpfProgAttach(...)\n\n// After all programs attached:\nif err := commit(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n#### `LoadCollection(logger *slog.Logger, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec, opts *CollectionOptions) (*ebpf.Collection, func() error, error)`\n\nLoads a collection into the kernel.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `logger`: Logger for debug output\n- `spec`: The compiled eBPF collection specification\n- `opts`: Load options\n\n**Returns:**\n- Collection: loaded maps and programs\n- Commit function: must be called after attaching programs\n- Error: if loading failed\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Validates all programs have specified types\n- Renames maps according to opts.MapRenames\n- Applies runtime constant overrides\n- Computes reachability and removes unused programs\n- Resolves tail calls\n- Removes unused maps\n- Handles map pinning and compatibility checks\n- Returns commit function for replacing pins\n\n### CollectionOptions\n\n```go\ntype CollectionOptions struct {\n    ebpf.CollectionOptions\n\n    // Replacements for datapath runtime configs (DECLARE_CONFIG)\n    Constants any\n\n    // Maps to be renamed during loading\n    // Key is key in CollectionSpec.Maps, value is new name\n    MapRenames []map[string]string\n\n    // Maps to be replaced with existing Map instances\n    // Used to replace maps with pre-configured ones\n    MapReplacements map[string]*Map\n\n    // Set of objects to keep during reachability pruning\n    Keep *set.Set[string]\n\n    // Path to write constants dump for debugging\n    ConfigDumpPath string\n}\n```\n\n**Constants Field:**\n- Pass a pointer to a populated struct from pkg/datapath/config\n- Used to override runtime-configurable values in eBPF code\n\n**MapRenames Field:**\n- Array of rename maps for flexibility\n- Later renames override earlier ones\n- Used to give maps unique names based on context\n\n**MapReplacements Field:**\n- Replace specific maps with pre-existing Map instances\n- Maps are specified by their CollectionSpec name\n- Useful for reusing maps across program loads\n\n### Pinning Behavior\n\n**Automatic Pinning:**\n- Maps marked as pinned in the spec are automatically loaded from opts.Maps.PinPath\n- Maps with incompatible existing pins are re-created and re-pinned\n- Maps with CILIUM_PIN_REPLACE flag have their pins replaced via commit function\n\n**Pin Replacement:**\n- Maps are not re-pinned immediately after loading\n- The returned commit function handles pin replacement\n- This allows multiple programs from same ELF to be attached before finalizing\n\n**Reasons for Pin Replacement:**\n1. Map incompatibility after upgrades/downgrades\n2. Tail call maps should not be repopulated with stale programs\n3. Maps with CILIUM_PIN_REPLACE flag set\n\n### Map Compatibility\n\nWhen opening a pinned map, Cilium checks:\n- Key size\n- Value size\n- Map type\n- Maximum entries\n- Flags\n\nIf any property differs, the map is considered incompatible and will be replaced.\n\n### Constants and Configuration\n\nRuntime configuration values can be defined in eBPF code using `DECLARE_CONFIG()` and overridden during loading:\n\n```go\nopts := &CollectionOptions{\n    Constants: &datapath.Config{\n        LBMapSize: 100000,\n        TupleSize: 48,\n    },\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Cache and Synchronization\n\n### Map Caching\n\nMaps can maintain a local cache of entries and track their synchronization state with the kernel.\n\n#### `WithCache() *Map`\n\nEnables caching on the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Stores all user-space inserted entries in a local cache\n- Tracks each entry's synchronization state (Insert, Delete, OK)\n- Automatically schedules error resolver if insertion fails\n- Enables periodic reconciliation of failed operations\n\n**Use Case:** When you need to track which operations failed and retry them\n\n### Pressure Metrics\n\n#### `WithPressureMetric(registry *metrics.Registry) *Map`\n\nEnables tracking of map pressure (utilization).\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Tracks map fill ratio as a metric\n- Reported only if over threshold (0.0 by default)\n- Metric updated with each map operation\n\n#### `WithPressureMetricThreshold(registry *metrics.Registry, threshold float64) *Map`\n\nEnables pressure metric with custom threshold.\n\n**Threshold:** Metric is only reported if pressure >= threshold\n\n### Builder Pattern\n\nAll `With*` methods return the Map instance, enabling fluent configuration:\n\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"name\", mapType, key, value, size, flags).\n    WithCache().\n    WithPressureMetric(registry).\n    WithEvents(config).\n    OpenOrCreate()\n```\n\n---\n\n## Utility Functions\n\n### Map Information\n\n#### `Name() string`\n\nReturns the basename of the map.\n\n#### `Path() (string, error)`\n\nReturns the filesystem path where the map is or will be pinned.\n\n#### `FD() int`\n\nReturns the file descriptor of the kernel map object.\n\n#### `IsOpen() bool`\n\nReturns whether the map is currently open.\n\n#### `Type() ebpf.MapType`\n\nReturns the map type (Hash, Array, etc.).\n\n#### `KeySize() uint32`\n\nReturns the size of key in bytes.\n\n#### `ValueSize() uint32`\n\nReturns the size of value in bytes.\n\n#### `MaxEntries() uint32`\n\nReturns the maximum number of entries.\n\n#### `Flags() uint32`\n\nReturns the creation flags.\n\n### Model Export\n\n#### `GetModel() *models.BPFMap`\n\nReturns an API model representation of the map for debugging/monitoring.\n\n**Includes:**\n- Map path\n- Cache entries (if cache enabled)\n- Key and value strings\n- Desired actions\n- Last error information\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Common Error Types\n\n**ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist:** Key not found in map (from ebpf-go)\n\n**ebpf.ErrMapIncompatible:** Map incompatible with existing pin (from ebpf-go)\n\n**unix.ENOSPC:** Buffer too small for batch operation (batch iterator auto-retries)\n\n**ErrMapNotOpened:** Map not opened yet (used by map ops)\n\n**ErrMaxLookup:** Iteration limit exceeded (unreliable iteration)\n\n### Error Resolver\n\nWhen caching is enabled, maps automatically schedule an error resolver that:\n- Runs periodically to reconcile cache and kernel state\n- Retries failed insertions\n- Retries failed deletions\n- Backs off exponentially with minimum 5-second intervals\n- Stops when all errors are resolved\n\n---\n\n## Best Practices\n\n1. **Map Creation:** Always pin maps for persistence across restarts\n2. **Error Handling:** Check for `ErrKeyNotExist` separately from other errors\n3. **Iteration:** Use `BatchIterator` for large maps for better performance\n4. **Concurrency:** Map operations are thread-safe but hold locks - keep callbacks short\n5. **Event Subscription:** Always cancel context to avoid resource leaks\n6. **Lock Awareness:** Never call `Delete()` from DumpCallback; use `DeleteLocked()`\n7. **Collection Loading:** Always call the commit function after attaching programs\n8. **Cleanup:** Close maps when done to release kernel resources\n9. **Testing:** Use `PrivilegedTest` and `CheckOrMountFS` for unit tests\n10. **Per-CPU Maps:** Verify value type implements `MapPerCPUValue` before iteration\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
